<h2><a id="post-149694-_492zsul47vlh"></a>BadSuccessor Overview</h2>
<p>BadSuccessor is a novel technique that enables a threat actor with sufficient privileges to compromise an Active Directory (AD) domain by misusing controlled delegated Managed Service Account (dMSA) objects.</p>
<p>Originally detailed in <a href="https://www.akamai.com/blog/security-research/abusing-dmsa-for-privilege-escalation-in-active-directory" target="_blank" rel="noopener">research published by Akamai</a>, this technique demonstrates how modifying a small set of attributes on a dMSA object under the attacker’s control can lead to privilege escalation within the environment. Publicly available tools have already been released to automate various steps involved in leveraging this technique, potentially lowering the barrier for its adoption.</p>
<p>We provide a comprehensive breakdown of the attack methodology, along with guidance on detection strategies and potential mitigations.</p>
<h2><a id="post-149694-_1f1ezd5rzu1d"></a>Understanding dMSAs</h2>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_uyoe9n27fn8z"></a>The Evolution of MSAs</h3>
<p>Windows has <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-authsod/5bb3e0c3-f6c1-4e2c-8c6d-0f54553b4ed9" target="_blank" rel="noopener">two basic types of accounts</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Machine accounts</li>
<li>User accounts</li>
</ul>
<p>In an AD environment, machine accounts represent hosts (servers or clients) that belong to a domain, while user accounts represent the users who log into and access the environment.</p>
<p>Service accounts are user accounts or machine accounts that <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/ad-ds/manage/understand-service-accounts" target="_blank" rel="noopener">provide a security context for services running on a Windows Server</a>. In other words, Windows services authenticate with service accounts. Windows relies on service accounts to run its various features.</p>
<p>With the release of Windows Server 2008 R2, Microsoft introduced Managed Service Accounts (MSAs) and group Managed Service Accounts (gMSAs) to simplify and enhance AD service account management.</p>
<p>MSAs and gMSAs are specialized service accounts designed to securely run services within an AD environment without the need for manual password handling. An MSA account is linked to a single computer, allowing only that machine to retrieve and use the account. Conversely, a gMSA account can be used by multiple computers, like clusters or server farms.</p>
<p>A key benefit of MSAs and gMSAs is that AD automatically manages their passwords. This involves generating strong, unique passwords and rotating them regularly, eliminating the need for human administrators to manage credentials. For example, when a service needs to access a domain resource, the Local Security Authority Subsystem Service (LSASS) uses the machine account to securely request the MSA or gMSA’s password. In this way, the password is handled in the AD and not directly by a user or an administrator.</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_79wsz4il0zn0"></a>Delegated Managed Service Accounts</h3>
<p>The dMSA is a new account type introduced in Windows Server 2025 to facilitate the migration of traditional service accounts to Managed Service Accounts. This process is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>An administrator creates a new dMSA object, which is intended to supersede the existing service account.</li>
<li>The administrator then initiates the migration, which sets the dMSA <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute to reference the original service account.</li>
<li>When the original service authenticates as the original service account, it triggers a Lightweight Directory Access Protocol (LDAP) modify request. This adds the machine account to the list of principals that are allowed to retrieve the dMSA password.</li>
<li>In the final step, the administrator completes the migration, which disables the original service account. The service continues to operate seamlessly using the dMSA.</li>
<li>Once a dMSA supersedes an existing account, any attempts to authenticate as that existing account using its password will be blocked. These authentication requests are redirected to the Local Security Authority (LSA) to authenticate using the dMSA. By then, the request has been granted all permissions that the original account had in the Active Directory, by the Key Distribution Center (KDC).</li>
</ul>
<p>While dMSAs are intended to prevent credential harvesting, dMSAs also create a privilege escalation path that attackers can exploit through the BadSuccessor technique.</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_fnyevtb6jed5"></a>dMSA Migration Flow</h3>
<p>The migration process of a traditional service account to a dMSA is triggered by an administrator using the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Start-ADServiceAccountMigration</span> PowerShell AD module command. The administrator passes the following values to the command:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/desktop/ldap/distinguished-names" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Distinguished Name (DN)</a> of the intended dMSA account</li>
<li>The DN of the superseded account</li>
</ul>
<p>As the migration continues, it changes several attributes of the normal service account as it transitions to a dSMA account, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attribute is set to 1 in the newly created dMSA.</li>
</ul>
<p>This attribute indicates the current state of the dMSA. <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/ad-ds/manage/delegated-managed-service-accounts/delegated-managed-service-accounts-overview#account-attributes-for-dmsa" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Microsoft's documentation</a> shows that 1 means the account migration has begun.</p>
<ul>
<li>The dMSA’s <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute is set to reference the superseded account.</li>
</ul>
<p>Next, the administrator initiates the<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"> Complete-ADServiceAccountMigration</span> command. This command disables the superseded account, and it changes the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-SupersededServiceAccountState</span> attribute values of the dMSA object to 2, indicating that the migration is complete.</p>
<p>Following this migration, any service that relies on the superseded account will use the dMSA instead, which now has all the permissions that the superseded account had.</p>
<h2><a id="post-149694-_y98v4rg1poog"></a>Technical Analysis: Bad Successor Technique and Tools</h2>
<p>This section demonstrates how attackers can use dMSAs to impersonate any domain user account, including the domain administrator, using the BadSuccessor technique.</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_z35s3l355ctu"></a>dMSA Misuse</h3>
<p>If an attacker or low-privileged user attempts to initiate the migration process for an existing service account, the operation will fail, because only administrative users can initiate migration. Instead of initiating the migration process, a potential attacker would create a dMSA and then change the same dMSA attributes that the valid migration process changes. This mimics a migration and has the same effect on the migrated account.</p>
<p>By default, only high-privileged users can create dMSAs under the default Managed Service Accounts container. However, other users can create dMSAs in other containers. This ultimately means that any domain user who has <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Create all child objects</span> or <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount</span> permissions on an organizational unit (OU) could potentially compromise the entire domain.</p>
<p>The following steps detail how an attacker could simulate the migration:</p>
<ul>
<li>Set the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute to contain the DN of the account the attacker wants to impersonate.</li>
<li>Set <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> to 2, to indicate that the migration process is complete.</li>
</ul>
<p>After changing these attributes and authenticating as the dMSA, the attacker obtains the full permissions of the superseded account.</p>
<p>Any user with sufficient permissions can execute this method in any AD environment managed by a Windows Server 2025 domain controller (DC).</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_qvvi2o6xwth"></a>BadSuccessor Simulation</h3>
<p>Before performing the actual attack, an attacker must ensure the compromised user has sufficient permissions to create all child objects or dMSAs. Akamai released a PowerShell script named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;"><a href="https://github.com/akamai/BadSuccessor/blob/main/Get-BadSuccessorOUPermissions.ps1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Get-BadSuccessorOUPermissions.ps1</a></span> that finds domain accounts that have the appropriate permissions on an OU to perform the BadSuccessor technique.</p>
<p>Figure 1 shows an example of Akamai's tool in action in a test AD environment. The output provides details of the objects in the domain that can be leveraged for BadSuccessor.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149711" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149711" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149711 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/figure-1-execution-of-get-badsuccessoroupermissio.png" alt="Screen showing Windows PowerShell with a command executed to get AD user permissions, displaying results for a specific user from a domain." width="800" height="153" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/figure-1-execution-of-get-badsuccessoroupermissio.png 1314w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/figure-1-execution-of-get-badsuccessoroupermissio-786x151.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/figure-1-execution-of-get-badsuccessoroupermissio-768x147.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149711" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 1. Executing <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Get-BadSuccessorOUPermissions.ps1</span> in our test environment.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the example from Figure 1, the results indicate that an account named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">test_weak</span> has the correct permissions to create a dMSA object under the OU <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">DelegatedOU</span>.</p>
<p>The enumeration tool performs the command shown in Figure 2 to retrieve OU DNs and their security descriptors.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149722" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149722" style="width: 784px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149722 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-387568-149694-2.png" alt="Screenshot of computer code text related to a PowerShell command, highlighted in blue and purple." width="784" height="50" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-387568-149694-2.png 784w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-387568-149694-2-768x49.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 784px) 100vw, 784px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149722" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 2. Command to retrieve OU DNs and their security descriptors.</figcaption></figure>
<p>After the tool retrieves the OU DNs and their security descriptors, it reviews the output to find the following rights:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Create Child: msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Create Child: All Objects</span></li>
</ul>
<p>The tool’s output reveals all users and OU pairs that can potentially be leveraged for the BadSuccessor technique.</p>
<p>Using a newly found account with the required permissions, an adversary can potentially perform the BadSuccessor technique using <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/powershell/module/activedirectory/?view=windowsserver2025-ps" target="_blank" rel="noopener">PowerShell's Active Directory Module</a> and <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/desktop/ldap/lightweight-directory-access-protocol-ldap-api" target="_blank" rel="noopener">LDAP</a>, as described in the <a href="https://www.akamai.com/blog/security-research/abusing-dmsa-for-privilege-escalation-in-active-directory" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Akamai article</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li>First, the attacker creates a dMSA under the found OU. We demonstrate this in Figure 3 by creating a dMSA object named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span>.</li>
</ul>
<figure id="attachment_149733" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149733" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149733 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-390092-149694-3.png" alt="Image depicts a computer code snippet on a dark background with text including PowerShell commands related to creating a new service account named &quot;attacker_0WSA&quot; and managing DNS and computer settings." width="800" height="146" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-390092-149694-3.png 1015w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-390092-149694-3-786x143.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-390092-149694-3-768x140.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149733" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 3. Commands to create a dMSA object under the found OU.</figcaption></figure>
<ul>
<li>Next, the attacker changes the attributes of the dMSA object to simulate the migration process. We demonstrated this in our test environment by setting the following values:
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute to contain the DN of the superseded account</li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> to 2, to indicate that the migration process is complete</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<figure id="attachment_149744" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149744" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149744 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-393583-149694-4.png" alt="Screenshot of computer code related to a dMSA object. " width="800" height="139" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-393583-149694-4.png 1045w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-393583-149694-4-786x136.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-393583-149694-4-768x133.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149744" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 4. Attributes of a dMSA object changed for the BadSuccessor technique.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Now that we know how the BadSuccessor technique works, let’s explore how different tools can automate an attack.</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_ku1hrv25pfd8"></a>SharpSuccessor</h3>
<p><a href="https://github.com/logangoins/SharpSuccessor/tree/master" target="_blank" rel="noopener">SharpSuccessor</a> is a proof of concept (PoC) hosted on a GitHub repository that automates the BadSuccessor technique. Figure 5 simulates an attack using a user account named <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">test_weak</span> in our test environment. This account has permissions to create a dMSA object under the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">DelegatedOU</span>.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149755" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149755" style="width: 1000px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149755 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5.png" alt="Screenshot of SharpSuccessor execution displaying commands for a malware attack simulation including logging in, adding a domain, and attempting to write and access attributes." width="1000" height="323" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5.png 2048w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5-786x254.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5-1920x621.png 1920w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5-768x248.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-396203-149694-5-1536x497.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149755" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 5. Execution of SharpSuccessor.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 6 shows that the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span> account is subsequently created in the OU.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149766" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149766" style="width: 1000px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149766 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-401049-149694-6.png" alt="Screenshot of the Active Directory Users and Computers management tool, displaying a list of folders including 'Users', 'Computers', and 'Domain Controllers.'" width="1000" height="528" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-401049-149694-6.png 1496w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-401049-149694-6-786x415.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-401049-149694-6-1326x700.png 1326w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-401049-149694-6-768x406.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149766" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 6. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span> created under <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">DelegatedOU</span>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 7 shows how <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">test_weak</span> changed the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attributes of <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span>. This simulates the completion of the migration.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149777" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149777" style="width: 600px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149777 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-405182-149694-7.png" alt="Screenshot of a software dialog box titled &quot;attacker_dMSA Properties&quot; displaying various system attributes and their corresponding values, primarily focused on security and user account settings. Two settings are highlighted. " width="600" height="573" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-405182-149694-7.png 788w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-405182-149694-7-461x440.png 461w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-405182-149694-7-734x700.png 734w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-405182-149694-7-768x733.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149777" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 7. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span> attributes <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span>.</figcaption></figure>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_w4wupgph9pv"></a>Pentest-Tools-Collection BadSuccessor Module</h3>
<p>The Pentest-Tools-Collection recently added a <a href="https://github.com/LuemmelSec/Pentest-Tools-Collection/blob/main/tools/ActiveDirectory/BadSuccessor.ps1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">BadSuccessor module</a> as one of its AD tools. This module has two modes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check mode</li>
<li>Exploit mode</li>
</ul>
<p>Like the enumeration tool we previously discussed, this module’s check mode enumerates an AD environment. This enumeration indicates whether the environment can be exploited using the BadSuccessor technique and what OU can be used for a successful attack.</p>
<p>Figure 8 shows the results of this module after we ran it in check mode in our test environment.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149788" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149788" style="width: 1000px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149788 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8.png" alt="Screenshot of PowerShell windows with queries being executed related to domain controls and system checks." width="1000" height="635" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8.png 1600w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8-693x440.png 693w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8-1102x700.png 1102w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8-768x488.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-409037-149694-8-1536x975.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149788" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 8. Executing Pentest-Tools-Collection's BadSuccessor module in check mode.</figcaption></figure>
<p>This module’s exploit mode creates a dMSA object and sets its attributes to falsely indicate that a migration process is complete. Figure 9 shows the use of this module in exploit mode automating the same BadSuccessor process previously shown in Figures 3 and 4.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149799" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149799" style="width: 750px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149799 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-413464-149694-9.png" alt="Command line interface showing the configuration of a user named 'test_weak' being granted impersonation rights on an 'Administrator' account within a domain environment." width="750" height="284" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-413464-149694-9.png 1010w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-413464-149694-9-786x297.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-413464-149694-9-768x290.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 750px) 100vw, 750px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149799" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 9. Executing Pentest-Tools-Collection's BadSuccessor module in exploit mode.</figcaption></figure>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_7x9kc7q9xmk8"></a>Domain Compromise</h3>
<p>After successfully executing the BadSuccessor technique, potential attackers can further exploit the domain using Rubeus, which <a href="https://www.akamai.com/blog/security-research/abusing-dmsa-for-privilege-escalation-in-active-directory#title-8738ec3891" target="_blank" rel="noopener">supports dMSA authentication</a>. Figure 10 illustrates some Rubeus commands using the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span> object in our test environment to gain access to privileged services in the domain.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149810" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149810" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149810 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-416557-149694-10.png" alt="Screenshot of a computer terminal displaying commands related to Rubues.exe on a Windows system, specifically for requesting and applying Kerberos tickets, involving entities such as a user named 'attacker', and domains ending in 'env20.local'." width="800" height="165" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-416557-149694-10.png 1047w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-416557-149694-10-786x162.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-416557-149694-10-768x158.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149810" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 10. Example of commands to use Rubeus to further exploit the domain in our test environment.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 11 shows that after executing these Rubeus commands, <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">test_weak</span> can now access the network share <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">C$</span> drive on the DC, which requires Domain Admin privileges.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149821" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149821" style="width: 600px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149821 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-419330-149694-11.png" alt="Screenshot of a Windows command prompt display showing directory listings with dates and times for folders such as Program Files, Program Files (x86), and Users." width="600" height="237" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-419330-149694-11.png 1034w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-419330-149694-11-786x310.png 786w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-419330-149694-11-768x303.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149821" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 11. <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">test_weak</span> account accessing the DC’s <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">C$</span> directory using the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">attacker_dMSA</span> object in our test environment.</figcaption></figure>
<h2><a id="post-149694-_r8mmtjim4hvx"></a>Detecting BadSuccessor Activity</h2>
<p>As presented in the <a href="https://www.akamai.com/blog/security-research/abusing-dmsa-for-privilege-escalation-in-active-directory#title-971c0073d4" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Akamai article</a>, the operations involved in BadSuccessor can be monitored via the following event IDs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Event ID 5137 — Tracks the creation of dMSA objects</li>
<li>Event ID 5136 — Tracks the modification of the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute</li>
<li>Event ID 2946 — Tracks the Ticket Granting Ticket (TGT) that is generated for a dMSA</li>
</ul>
<p>But we propose an alternative way to track BadSuccessor activity and the footprints that it leaves behind; by leveraging Event ID 4662.</p>
<p>When a user creates a dMSA object, the initiating user or process requires and uses the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">CreateChild</span> <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/kernel/access-rights" target="_blank" rel="noopener">access rights</a> on the OU. Figure 12 shows how dMSA object creation using the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">CreateChild</span> access rights is reflected in Event ID 4662 (An operation was performed on an object).</p>
<figure id="attachment_149832" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149832" style="width: 564px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149832 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-423062-149694-12.png" alt="Event Properties window showing details of event 4662, Microsoft Windows security auditing. Fields include Account Name, Security ID, Object Type, Handle ID, Operation Type, and other specific identifiers, highlighted with a red box around the Additional Information. " width="564" height="610" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-423062-149694-12.png 564w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-423062-149694-12-407x440.png 407w" sizes="(max-width: 564px) 100vw, 564px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149832" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 12. Event ID 4662 that audits the dMSA creation.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The same Event ID is generated when a user with sufficient access rights modifies the following two attributes in the properties of the dMSA object.</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">2f5c138a-bd38-4016-88b4-0ec87cbb4919</span> represents <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">a0945b2b-57a2-43bd-b327-4d112a4e8bd1</span> represents <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span></li>
</ul>
<p>Changing the above dMSA attributes triggers the event shown in Figure 13.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149843" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149843" style="width: 559px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149843 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-425751-149694-13.png" alt="Event Properties window showing details of event 4662, Microsoft Windows security auditing. Fields include Account Name, Security ID, Object Type, Handle ID, Operation Type, and other specific identifiers, highlighted with a red box around the Security ID, Account Name, Access Mask, Properties and more. " width="559" height="655" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-425751-149694-13.png 559w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-425751-149694-13-376x440.png 376w" sizes="(max-width: 559px) 100vw, 559px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149843" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 13. Event ID 4662 that audits the change to the dMSA’s attributes.</figcaption></figure>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_smads0vis9uk"></a>Legitimate dMSA Migration Process Footprints</h3>
<p>To better detect BadSuccessor, we must also know the differences between the footprints of malicious dMSA activity and legitimate dMSA migration. Only Administrative users can legitimately migrate service accounts to dMSA objects. To detect BadSuccessor activity, we must search for unprivileged users who have created a dMSA and then accessed the object’s specific attributes with the Access Mask value of <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">0x20</span> as shown in Figure 13.</p>
<p>A slightly different footprint is created when a privileged user creates a dMSA legitimately and then migrates a service account. According to <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/identity/ad-ds/manage/delegated-managed-service-accounts/delegated-managed-service-accounts-set-up-dmsa" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Microsoft's guide</a>, only a privileged user can create a dMSA under the OU <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Managed Service Account</span>. The Event 4662 log entry in Figure 14 shows an Administrator user creating a child object (the dMSA) in the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Managed Service Account</span> OU.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149854" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149854" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149854 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-429017-149694-14.png" alt="Event Properties window showing details of event 4662, Microsoft Windows security auditing." width="800" height="721" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-429017-149694-14.png 1099w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-429017-149694-14-488x440.png 488w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-429017-149694-14-777x700.png 777w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-429017-149694-14-768x692.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149854" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 14. Event ID 4662 that documents the creation of a legitimate dMSA.</figcaption></figure>
<p>A legitimate migration uses an initial <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attribute with a value of 1. Figure 15 shows that the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attribute was changed in the first step of the migration process, while Figure 16 shows it was changed to 1.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149865" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149865" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149865 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-433083-149694-15.png" alt="Event Properties window showing details of event 4662, Microsoft Windows security auditing. A red box highlights the last item in the Properties list. " width="800" height="715" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-433083-149694-15.png 1117w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-433083-149694-15-492x440.png 492w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-433083-149694-15-783x700.png 783w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-433083-149694-15-768x686.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149865" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 15. Event ID 4662 that audits the first step of dMSA account migration, where the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attribute is changed.</figcaption></figure>
<figure id="attachment_149876" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149876" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149876 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-436824-149694-16.png" alt="Screenshot of Microsoft Windows security auditing event detail, focusing on the LDAP Display Name 'msDs-DelegatedServiceAccount' with its value set to 1." width="800" height="777" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-436824-149694-16.png 1095w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-436824-149694-16-453x440.png 453w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-436824-149694-16-720x700.png 720w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-436824-149694-16-768x746.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149876" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 16. Event ID 5136 that audits the change of the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAStat</span>e dMSA object attribute to 1.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Figure 17 shows the last step that consists of changing the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> attribute to 2, and changing the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attribute to the superseded account.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149887" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149887" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149887 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-440973-149694-17.png" alt="Event Properties window showing details of a security audit for Event 4662. The object accessed is managed by the account &quot;ENVO\Administrator&quot; and the operation involved writing properties. A specific GUID identifier is highlighted in red." width="800" height="707" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-440973-149694-17.png 1130w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-440973-149694-17-498x440.png 498w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-440973-149694-17-792x700.png 792w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-440973-149694-17-768x679.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149887" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 17. Event ID 4662 that audits the changes made to the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-DelegatedMSAState</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink</span> attributes.</figcaption></figure>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_cugw0gmfi5a6"></a>Enabling Auditing</h3>
<p>To identify the attack footprint and conduct detection activities, auditing must be enabled. Figure 18 shows an example of a relevant auditing interface.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149898" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149898" style="width: 893px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149898 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-444423-149694-18.png" alt="Screenshot of a computer interface for managing user permissions with various options for types of permissions like 'Read all' and 'Modify permissions', and an arrow pointing to a dropdown list labeled 'Assign to' with the selected option." width="893" height="529" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-444423-149694-18.png 893w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-444423-149694-18-743x440.png 743w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-444423-149694-18-768x455.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 893px) 100vw, 893px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-149898" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 18. Example of auditing enablement on Windows Server 2025.</figcaption></figure>
<h2><a id="post-149694-_6kajjrwpgjuu"></a>Conclusion</h2>
<p>We examined the BadSuccessor technique and explored how, under certain conditions, adversaries can exploit the newly introduced dMSAs in a Windows Server 2025 DC to compromise the domain. We also analyzed the operational footprints left by this activity and proposed a novel detection strategy to identify such attacks.</p>
<p>Given how effective this attack can be, we strongly recommend closely monitoring Microsoft’s updates to understand available mitigation strategies and to properly configure all permissions — particularly those related to the BadSuccessor attack.</p>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_lqzcx8cug942"></a>Palo Alto Networks Protections</h3>
<p>Palo Alto Networks customers can leverage a variety of product protections and updates to identify and defend against this threat.</p>
<p>One such product is Palo Alto Networks <a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/p/XSIAM" target="_blank" rel="noopener">XSIAM</a>, which can detect BadSuccessor activity if Windows security auditing is enabled on the dMSA. Our <a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/r/Cortex-XSIAM/Cortex-XSIAM-Documentation/Microsoft-Windows-security-auditing-setup" target="_blank" rel="noopener">security auditing guide for Microsoft Windows systems</a> provides information on how to configure the <a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/r/Cortex-XSIAM/Cortex-XSIAM-Documentation/Enable-auditing-access-to-AD-domain-objects-4662" target="_blank" rel="noopener">required auditing</a> on Windows Server 2025.</p>
<p>Figure 19 shows an example of a “Possible Privilege Escalation using delegated MSA account attempt” in XSIAM.</p>
<figure id="attachment_149909" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-149909" style="width: 818px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-149909 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/word-image-447143-149694-19.png" alt="Screenshot of Cortex XDR cybersecurity dashboard displaying details about a potential Privilege Escalation incident using Delegated MSA account in a Windows environment. Example of a Cortex XDR alert for “Possible privilege escalation using delegated MSA account attempt.”</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/p/XDR">Cortex XDR</a> and <a href="https://docs-cortex.paloaltonetworks.com/p/XSIAM" target="_blank" rel="noopener">XSIAM</a> detect user and credential-based threats by analyzing user activity from multiple data sources including endpoints, network firewalls, AD, identity and access management solutions, and cloud workloads. Cortex builds behavioral profiles of user activity over time with machine learning. By comparing new activity to past activity, peer activity and the expected behavior of the entity, Cortex detects anomalous activity indicative of credential-based attacks.</p>

Learn more about the <a href="https://www.cyberthreatalliance.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cyber Threat Alliance</a>.</p>

<h2><a id="post-149694-_ftx9zzz44k46"></a>Appendix</h2>
<h3><a id="post-149694-_vgezw6a4uez"></a>Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting Queries</h3>
<p>The Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting team has created queries that can help defenders identify potential signs of dMSA misuse and use of SharpSuccessor.</p>
<p>Assuming that all auditing has been enabled and event logs are being properly ingested, the query provided below can be used to identify potential signs of SharpSuccessor execution.</p>
<p>As SharpSuccessor creates a computer account, hunters can correlate SubjectLogonIDs to identify relevant events. Event ID 4741 indicates that a computer account was created, and Event ID 4662 shows that an operation was performed — in this case, dMSA creation. Then, hunters can enrich the details of the user account that performed the action, by correlating Event ID 4624 to pull in information such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Workstation name</li>
<li>IP address</li>
<li>Logon type</li>
</ul>
<p>We recommend running this query on smaller time frames, given the multiple joins and alter commands leveraged.</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
dataset = xdr_data

// Identify any object access/modification events for the msDS-DelegatedManagerServiceAccount object type

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields, action_evtlog_message, event_timestamp

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4662

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter ObjectServer = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectServer

| alter ObjectType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectType

| alter ObjectName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectName

| alter AdditionalInfo2 = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AdditionalInfo2

| alter OperationType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OperationType

| alter AccessList = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AccessList

| alter AccessMask = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AccessMask

// msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount Object Type

| filter ObjectType = "%{0feb936f-47b3-49f2-9386-1dedc2c23765}" and AccessMask = "0x20"

// Join on Event ID 4741 by SubjectLogonID to identify the machine account name that was created.

| join type = inner conflict_strategy = left (

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_description, event_type, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4741

// Field extraction

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter TargetUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserName

| alter TargetDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetDomainName

| alter SamAccountName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SamAccountName

| alter DnsHostName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DnsHostName

| fields _time as comp_time, agent_hostname as comp_hostname, SubjectDomainName as comp_SubjectDomainName, SubjectUserName as comp_SubjectUserName, SubjectLogonId as comp_SubjectLogonId, SubjectUserSid as comp_SubjectUserSid, TargetUserName, SamAccountName, DnsHostName

) as cmpcreate cmpcreate.comp_hostname = agent_hostname and cmpcreate.comp_SubjectUserName = SubjectUserName and cmpcreate.comp_SubjectLogonId = SubjectLogonId and cmpcreate.comp_SubjectUserSid = SubjectUserSid

// Join on Event ID 4624 to enrich authentication activity that performed the machine account creation, and dMSA creation

| join type = left (

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4624

// Extract relevant fields

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter TargetDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetDomainName

| alter TargetUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserName

| alter TargetUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserSid

| alter TargetLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetLogonId

| alter IpAddress = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpAddress

| alter IpPort = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpPort

| alter LogonType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; LogonType

| alter WorkstationName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; WorkstationName

| filter TargetUserName !~= "(?:(?:(?:DWM|UMFD)-\d)|(?:NETWORK SERVICE)|(?:LOCAL SERVICE)|(?:ANONYMOUS LOGON)|(?:SYSTEM)|\w+\$$)"

| fields agent_hostname as auth_hostname, TargetUserName as auth_username, TargetLogonId as auth_logonID, TargetUserSid as auth_usersid, IpAddress, WorkstationName, LogonType

) as auth auth.auth_hostname = agent_hostname and auth.auth_username = SubjectUserName and auth.auth_logonID = SubjectLogonId and auth.auth_usersid = SubjectUserSid

| fields _time, agent_hostname, SubjectDomainName, SubjectUserSid, SubjectUserName, SubjectLogonId, OperationType, ObjectType, ObjectName, comp_time, TargetUserName, SamAccountName, DnsHostName, LogonType, IpAddress, WorkstationName</textarea></div>

						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480-1"><span class="crayon-i">dataset</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">xdr_data</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480-3"><span class="crayon-c">// Identify any object access/modification events for the msDS-DelegatedManagerServiceAccount object type</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480-4">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6893ec251dafc678264480-5"><span class="crayon-sy">|</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">fields </span><span class="crayon-i">_time</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">agent_hostname</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">event_type</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">action_evtlog_event_id</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">action_evtlog_data_fields</span><span <!-- [Format Time: 0.0018 seconds] -->
<p>For customers who have enabled auditing and are ingesting Event ID 5136, the following query can be used to identify creation of dMSAs.</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6893ec251db1b581830232" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
// Description: Identify creation of a dMSA

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 5136

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter AppCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AppCorrelationID

| alter AttributeLDAPDisplayName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeLDAPDisplayName

| alter AttributeSyntaxOID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeSyntaxOID

| alter AttributeValue = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeValue

| alter DSName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSName

| alter DSType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSType

| alter ObjectClass = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectClass

| alter ObjectDN = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectDN

| alter ObjectGUID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectGUID

| alter OpCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OpCorrelationID

| alter OperationType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OperationType

// ObjectGUID is the MsDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount and the attribute value of 2 where the operation is a Value Add

| filter ObjectClass = "msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount" and AttributeLDAPDisplayName = "msDS-DelegatedMSAState" and AttributeValue = "2" and OperationType = "%%14674"

// Query to pull in the authentication activity that performed the object access/modification

| join type = left (

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4624

// Extract relevant fields

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter TargetDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetDomainName

| alter TargetUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserName

| alter TargetUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserSid

| alter TargetLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetLogonId

| alter IpAddress = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpAddress

| alter IpPort = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpPort

| alter LogonType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; LogonType

| alter WorkstationName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; WorkstationName

| filter TargetUserName !~= "(?:(?:(?:DWM|UMFD)-\d)|(?:NETWORK SERVICE)|(?:LOCAL SERVICE)|(?:ANONYMOUS LOGON)|(?:SYSTEM)|\w+\$$)"

| fields agent_hostname as auth_hostname, TargetUserName as auth_username, TargetLogonId as auth_logonID, TargetUserSid as auth_usersid, IpAddress, WorkstationName, LogonType

) as auth auth.auth_hostname = agent_hostname and auth.auth_username = SubjectUserName and auth.auth_logonID = SubjectLogonId and auth.auth_usersid = SubjectUserSid

| fields _time, agent_hostname, SubjectDomainName, SubjectUserName, SubjectUserSid, SubjectLogonId, ObjectDN, ObjectGUID, AttributeLDAPDisplayName, AttributeValue, LogonType, IpAddress, WorkstationName</textarea></div>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p>Additionally, the following query can be used to identify which gMSA or standalone Managed Service Account (sMSA) account the new dMSA should supersede:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6893ec251db20573401607" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
// Description: Identify which gMSA/sMSA account the new dMSA should supersede

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 5136

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter AppCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AppCorrelationID

| alter AttributeLDAPDisplayName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeLDAPDisplayName

| alter AttributeSyntaxOID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeSyntaxOID

| alter AttributeValue = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeValue

| alter DSName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSName

| alter DSType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSType

| alter ObjectClass = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectClass

| alter ObjectDN = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectDN

| alter ObjectGUID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectGUID

| alter OpCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OpCorrelationID

| alter OperationType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OperationType

// ObjectGUID is the MsDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount and the AttributeLDAPDisplayName is msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink where a value was added

| filter ObjectClass = "msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount" and AttributeLDAPDisplayName = "msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink" and OperationType = "%%14674"

// Query to pull in the authentication activity that performed the object access/modification

| join type = left (

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4624

// Extract relevant fields

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter TargetDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetDomainName

| alter TargetUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserName

| alter TargetUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserSid

| alter TargetLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetLogonId

| alter IpAddress = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpAddress

| alter IpPort = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpPort

| alter LogonType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; LogonType

| alter WorkstationName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; WorkstationName

| filter TargetUserName !~= "(?:(?:(?:DWM|UMFD)-\d)|(?:NETWORK SERVICE)|(?:LOCAL SERVICE)|(?:ANONYMOUS LOGON)|(?:SYSTEM)|\w+\$$)"

| fields agent_hostname as auth_hostname, TargetUserName as auth_username, TargetLogonId as auth_logonID, TargetUserSid as auth_usersid, IpAddress, WorkstationName, LogonType

) as auth auth.auth_hostname = agent_hostname and auth.auth_username = SubjectUserName and auth.auth_logonID = SubjectLogonId and auth.auth_usersid = SubjectUserSid

| fields _time, agent_hostname, SubjectDomainName, SubjectUserName, SubjectUserSid, SubjectLogonId, ObjectDN, ObjectGUID, AttributeLDAPDisplayName, AttributeValue, LogonType, IpAddress, WorkstationName</textarea></div>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p>The following queries can be used independently. Alternatively, they can be combined in a single query that will show details of the new dMSA, the new account name and the superseded accounts.</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6893ec251db24141659385" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
// Description: Identify creation of dMSA

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 5136

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter AppCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AppCorrelationID

| alter AttributeLDAPDisplayName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeLDAPDisplayName

| alter AttributeSyntaxOID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeSyntaxOID

| alter AttributeValue = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeValue

| alter DSName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSName

| alter DSType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; DSType

| alter ObjectClass = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectClass

| alter ObjectDN = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectDN

| alter ObjectGUID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectGUID

| alter OpCorrelationID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OpCorrelationID

| alter OperationType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OperationType

// ObjectGUID is the MsDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount and the attribute value of 2 where the operation is a Value Add

| filter ObjectClass = "msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount" and AttributeLDAPDisplayName = "msDS-DelegatedMSAState" and AttributeValue = "2" and OperationType = "%%14674"

// Attempt to join on a 5136 event where the dMSA that was created shows the value of the superseded sMSA/gMSA account

| join type = left (

// Description: Identify which gMSA/sMSA account the new dMSA should supersede

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 5136

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter AttributeLDAPDisplayName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeLDAPDisplayName

| alter AttributeValue = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; AttributeValue

| alter ObjectClass = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectClass

| alter ObjectDN = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectDN

| alter ObjectGUID = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; ObjectGUID

| alter OperationType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; OperationType

// ObjectGUID is the MsDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount and the AttributeLDAPDisplayName is msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink where a value was added

| filter ObjectClass = "msDS-DelegatedManagedServiceAccount" and AttributeLDAPDisplayName = "msDS-ManagedAccountPrecededByLink" and OperationType = "%%14674"

| fields SubjectDomainName, SubjectLogonId, SubjectUserName, SubjectUserSid, AttributeValue as SupersededAttributeValue, ObjectGUID, AttributeLDAPDisplayName as supersededAttributeLDAPDisplayName

) as superseded superseded.SubjectDomainName = SubjectDomainName and superseded.SubjectUserName = SubjectUserName and superseded.ObjectGUID = ObjectGUID and superseded.SubjectLogonId = SubjectLogonId and superseded.SubjectUserSid = SubjectUserSid

// Query to pull in the authentication activity that performed the object access/modification

| join type = left (

dataset = xdr_data

| fields _time, agent_hostname, event_type, action_evtlog_event_id, action_evtlog_data_fields

| filter event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and action_evtlog_event_id = 4624

// Extract relevant fields

| alter SubjectDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectDomainName

| alter SubjectUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserSid

| alter SubjectUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectUserName

| alter SubjectLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; SubjectLogonId

| alter TargetDomainName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetDomainName

| alter TargetUserName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserName

| alter TargetUserSid = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetUserSid

| alter TargetLogonId = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; TargetLogonId

| alter IpAddress = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpAddress

| alter IpPort = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; IpPort

| alter LogonType = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; LogonType

| alter WorkstationName = action_evtlog_data_fields -&gt; WorkstationName

| filter TargetUserName !~= "(?:(?:(?:DWM|UMFD)-\d)|(?:NETWORK SERVICE)|(?:LOCAL SERVICE)|(?:ANONYMOUS LOGON)|(?:SYSTEM)|\w+\$$)"

| fields agent_hostname as auth_hostname, TargetUserName as auth_username, TargetLogonId as auth_logonID, TargetUserSid as auth_usersid, IpAddress, WorkstationName, LogonType

) as auth auth.auth_hostname = agent_hostname and auth.auth_username = SubjectUserName and auth.auth_logonID = SubjectLogonId and auth.auth_usersid = SubjectUserSid

| fields _time, agent_hostname, SubjectDomainName, SubjectUserName, SubjectUserSid, SubjectLogonId, ObjectDN, ObjectGUID, AttributeLDAPDisplayName, AttributeValue, SupersededAttributeValue, SupersededAttributeValue, LogonType, IpAddress, WorkstationName</textarea></div>

<h3><a id="post-149694-_abkrql69dzec"></a>XDR Alerts and MITRE Techniques</h3>
<p>Table 1 lists the Cortex XDR alerts and the associated MITRE ATT&amp;CK techniques these alerts detect.</p>
<table style="width: 100%;">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="text-align: center;"><b>Alert Name</b></td>
<td style="text-align: center;"><b>Alert Source</b></td>
<td style="text-align: center;"><b>ATT&amp;CK Technique</b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Possible Privilege Escalation using Delegated MSA account</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">XDR Analytics, Identity Analytics</span></td>
<td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1098/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Account Manipulation (T1098)</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> </span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Rare machine account creation</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">XDR Analytics BIOC, Identity Analytics</span></td>
<td><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1136" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Create Account (T1136)</span></a><b> </b></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Table 1. Relevant alerts and MITRE techniques.</span></p>

<script>

(function($) {
	// Migrated from the unit42-v5 + Modifications
	var subscribeSuccess = false;
	var email = document.getElementById('newsletter-email');
	var subscription_form = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form');
	var subscription_form_button = document.getElementById('unit42footerSubscription_form_button');
	window.captchaComplete = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = true;
		if ($(mail).val() != '' && isEmail($(mail).val())) {
			$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
		}
		setTimeout(function() {
			$(email).focus();
			$('.g-recaptcha iframe').attr('tabindex', '-1');
		}, 100)
	}
	window.captchaExpires = function() {
		subscribeSuccess = false;
		$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
	} 
	$(subscription_form).submit(function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		e.stopImmediatePropagation();
		updateEmailMask();
		var success = true;
		var form = $(this);
		var mail = form.find('input[name="Email"]');
		
		if (mail.val() === '') {
			mail.addClass('has-error');
			showError(1);
			success = false;	
		}  else if (!isEmail(mail.val())){
			showError(2);
			success = false;
		}
		else {
			mail.removeClass('has-error');
			$('.error-mail').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (!subscribeSuccess) {
			$('.error-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
		} else {
			$('.error-recaptcha').addClass('d-none');
		}

		if (success && subscribeSuccess) {
			$.ajax({
				type: 'POST',
				url: form.attr('action'),
				data: form.serialize(),
				beforeSend: function() {
                 form.find('button').addClass('is-loading');
    			},
				success: function(msg) {
					form.find('.form-success-message').html('<p class="success-message">You have been successfully subscribed</p>');
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					$(email).val('');
					clearError();
				},
				error: function(jqXHR, textStatus, errorThrown) {
					$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled', true);
					form.find('button').removeClass('is-loading');
					
				}
			});
		}
		return false;
	});
	function showError(error_type){
		if(error_type == 1) {
			$('.error-mail').text("Please enter the email address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		} else if(error_type == 2){
			$('.error-mail').text("Please provide a valid e-mail address.").addClass('error-show');
			$(subscription_form_button).addClass('is-disabled');
		}	
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
	}
	function clearError(){
		$('.error-mail').text("").removeClass('error-show');;
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-loading');
		$(subscription_form_button).removeClass('is-disabled');
	}
	
	$(email).on('input', function (event) { 
		var email = $(this).val();
		if (isEmail(email) ) {			
			clearError();
		} else if(email == ""){
			clearError();
		} else{
			showError(2);			  
		}
    });

	function isEmail(email) {
		var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
		return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
	}
	
	var captcha_loaded = false;
         if(!captcha_loaded){
            // recaptcha on foucs call
            $(document).on('change paste keyup', '#newsletter-email', function () {
               if($('.g-recaptcha').hasClass('d-none')){
                $('.g-recaptcha').removeClass('d-none');
               }
               if(!captcha_loaded ){
                  captcha_loaded  = true;
                  // trigger loading api.js (recaptcha.js) script
                  var head = document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
                  var script = document.createElement('script');
                  script.type = 'text/javascript';
                  script.src = 'https://www.google.com/recaptcha/api.js?hl=en_US';
                  head.appendChild(script);
               }
            });
        }
	
	function updateEmailMask() {
		var email = $("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='Email']").val();
		if (email && email.trim() != '') {
			var maskedEmail = maskEmailAddress(email);
			$("#unit42footerSubscription_form input[name='emailFormMask']").val(maskedEmail);
		}
	}

	function maskEmailAddress (emailAddress) {
		function mask(str) {
			var strLen = str.length;
			if (strLen > 4) {
				return str.substr(0, 1) + str.substr(1, strLen - 1).replace(/\w/g, '*') + str.substr(-1,1);
			}
			return str.replace(/\w/g, '*');
		}
		return emailAddress.replace(/([\w.]+)@([\w.]+)(\.[\w.]+)/g, function (m, p1, p2, p3) {
			return mask(p1) + '@' + mask(p2) + p3;
		});

		return emailAddress;
	}

}(jQuery));
//# sourceMappingURL=main.js.map
	
</script>

<script type="text/javascript">
	$(document).ready(function(){
		$("html").on("click", ".language-btn", function () {
			$(this).toggleClass("expand");
			$(".language-dropdown").toggleClass("expand");
		});

		$("html").on("click", "body", function (b) {
			if (!$(b.target).is(".language-btn")) {
				$(".language-btn").removeClass("expand");
				$(".language-dropdown").removeClass("expand");
			}
		});
	});
</script>

	var isProcessing = false; 
    function alter_ul_post_values(obj,post_id,ul_type){
	
		if (isProcessing)    
		return;  
		isProcessing = true;   
		var like_nonce = jQuery('#_wpnonce').val();
		jQuery(obj).find("span").html("..");
                jQuery.ajax({
                    type: "POST",
                    url: "https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/plugins/like-dislike-counter-for-posts-pages-and-comments/ajax_counter.php",
                    data: "post_id="+post_id+"&up_type="+ul_type+"&ul_nonce="+like_nonce,
                    success: function(msg){
                            jQuery(obj).find("span").html(msg);
                            isProcessing = false; 
                            jQuery(obj).find('svg').children('path').attr('stroke','#0050FF');
                            jQuery(obj).removeClass('idc_ul_cont_not_liked idc_ul_cont_not_liked_inner');
                    }
 		});
	}

    }
    return out;
  };
  return self
  }());
}

function loadScript(url, defer){
    var script1 = document.createElement('script');
    script1.setAttribute('type', 'text/javascript');
    script1.setAttribute('src',url);
    if(defer == true){
        script1.setAttribute('defer','defer');
    }
    document.head.appendChild(script1);
}
function loadScript1(url, callback){

    var script = document.createElement("script")
    script.type = "text/javascript";
    if (script.readyState){  //IE
        script.onreadystatechange = function(){
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" || script.readyState == "complete"){
                script.onreadystatechange = null;
                callback();
            }
        };
    } else {  //Others
        script.onload = function(){
            callback();
        };
    }
    script.src = url;
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
}

    }, 3000);
	}
}

document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function() {
  // Find all the forms on the page
  var forms = document.getElementsByTagName("form");

  // Loop through each form
  for (var i = 0; i < forms.length; i++) {
    var form = forms[i];

    // Check if the hidden input field already exists
    var requestInput = form.querySelector("input[name='web_unit42_req_id']");
    if (!requestInput) {
      // Create a hidden input element if it doesn't exist
      requestInput = document.createElement("input");
      requestInput.type = "hidden";
      requestInput.name = "web_unit42_req_id";
      requestInput.id = "web_unit42_req_id";

      // Append the hidden field to the form
      form.appendChild(requestInput);
    }
  }
});

// Assign the onCheqResponse function to the window object to handle events from any form
window.onCheqResponse = function(encryptedMessage, requestID) {
  // Find all the forms on the page
  var forms = document.getElementsByTagName("form");

  for (var i = 0; i < forms.length; i++) {
    var form = forms[i];
    var requestInput = form.querySelector("input[name='web_unit42_req_id']");
    if (requestInput) {
      requestInput.value = requestID;
    }
  }
};
